"import { Binding, Context, Logger, omit, Schema, Service, Time, User } from 'koishi'\nimport { Client } from '@koishijs/console'\nimport { createHash } from 'crypto'\nimport { resolve } from LoginToken\n  }\n}\n\ndeclare module '@koishijs/console' {\n  interface Client {\n    auth?: Auth\n  }\n\n  namespace Console {\n    interface Services {\n      user: DataService<AuthData>\n    }\n  }\n\n  interface Events {\n    'login/platform'(this: Client, platform: string, pid: string): Promise<UserLogin>\n    'login/password'(this: Client, name: string, password: string): void\n 'user/update'(this: Client, data: UserUpdate): void\n    'user/logout'(this: Client): void\n  }\n}\n\nexport interface LoginToken {\n  inc: number\n  id: number\n  type: LoginType\n  token: string\n  expiredAt: number\n  createdAt: Date\n  lastUsedAt: Date\n  userAgent: string\n  address: string\n}\n\nexport type Auth =\n  & Pick<LoginToken, 'token' | 'expiredAt'>\n  & Pick<User, 'id' | 'name' | 'authority' | 'config'>\n\ninterface AuthData extends Auth {\n  tokens: Omit<LoginToken, 'token' | 'id'>[]\n  bindings: Omit<Binding, 'aid'>[]\n}\n\ntype LoginType = 'platform' | 'password' | 'token'\n\nconst logger = new Logger('auth')\n\nconst letters = '0123456789abcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyzABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZ'\n\nexport function randomId(length = 40) {\n  return Array(length).fill(0).map(() => letters[Math.floor(Math.random() * letters.length)]).join('')\n}\n\nexport interface UserLogin extends Pick<User, 'id' | 'name'> {\n  token: string\n  expiredAt: number\n}\n\nexport type UserUpdate = Partial<Pick<User, 'name' | 'password' | 'config'>>\n\nfunction toHash(password: string) {\n  return createHash('sha256').update(password).digest('hex')\n}\n\nclass AuthService extends Service {\n  static using = ['console', 'database'] as const\n\n  constructor(ctx: Context, private config: AuthService.Config) {\n    super(ctx, 'auth')\n\n    ctx.model.extend('user', {\n      password: 'string(255)',\n      config: {\n        type: 'json',\n        length: 65535,\n        initial: null,\n      },\n    })\n\n    ctx.model.extend('token', {\n      inc: 'unsigned',\n      id: 'unsigned',\n      type: 'string(255)',\n      token: 'string(255)',\n      expiredAt: 'unsigned(20)',\n      createdAt: 'timestamp',\n      lastUsedAt: 'timestamp',\n      userAgent: 'string(255)',\n      address: 'string(255)',\n    }, {\n      primary: 'inc',\n      autoInc: true,\n      unique: ['token'],\n    })\n\n    ctx.console.addEntry({\n      dev: resolve(__dirname, '../client/index.ts'),\n      prod: resolve(__dirname, '../dist'),\n    })\n\n    this.initLogin()\n  }\n\n  async start() {\n    const { enabled, username, password } = this.config.admin\n    if (!enabled) return\n    logger.info('creating admin account')\n    await this.ctx.database.upsert('user', [{\n      id: 0,\n      name: username,\n      authority: 5,\n      password: toHash(password),\n      createdAt: new Date(),\n    }])\n  }\n\n  async setAuth(client: Client, auth = client.auth, passive = false) {\n    client.auth = auth\n    if (passive) return\n    if (auth) {\n      const bindings = await this.ctx.database.get('binding', { aid: auth.id })\n      bindings.forEach(binding => delete binding.aid)\n      const tokens = await this.ctx.database.get('token', { id: auth.id })\n      tokens.reverse().forEach(login => (delete login.id, delete login.token))\n      client.send({ type: 'data', body: { key: 'user', value: { ...auth, bindings, tokens } } })\n    } else {\n      client.send({ type: 'data', body: { key: 'user', value: null } })\n    }\n    client.ctx.emit('console/connection', client)\n    client.refresh()\n  }\n\n  async createToken(client: Client, type: LoginType, user: Pick<User, 'id' | 'name' | 'authority' | 'config'>) {\n    const { headers, socket } = client.request\n    const createdAt = new Date()\n    const lastUsedAt = new Date()\n    const userAgent = headers['user-agent']?.toString()\n    const address = headers['x-forwarded-for']?.toString() || socket.remoteAddress\n    const expiredAt = Date.now() + this.config.authTokenExpire\n    const token = randomId()\n    await this.ctx.database.create('token', { id: user.id, type, expiredAt, token, createdAt, lastUsedAt, userAgent, address })\n    await this.setAuth(client, { ...user, expiredAt, token })\n  }\n\n  initLogin() {\n    const self = this\n    const { ctx, config } = this\n    const states: Record<string, [string, number, Client]> = {}\n\n    ctx.console.addListener('login/password', async function (name, password) {\n      password = toHash(password)\n      const [user] = await ctx.database.get('user', { name }, ['password', 'name', 'id', 'authority', 'config'])\n      if (!user || user.password !== password) throw new Error('用户名或密码错误。')\n      await self.createToken(this, 'password', omit(user, ['password']))\n    })\n\n    ctx.console.addListener('login/token', async function (aid, token) {\n      const [data] = await ctx.database.get('token', { id: aid, token }, ['expiredAt'])\n      if (!data || data.expiredAt <= Date.now()) throw new Error('令牌已失效。')\n      const [user] = await ctx.database.get('user', { id: aid }, ['id', 'name', 'authority', 'config'])\n      if (!user) throw new Error('用户不存在。')\n      await ctx.database.set('token', { token }, { lastUsedAt: new Date() })\n      await self.setAuth(this, { ...user, ...data, token })\n    })\n\n    ctx.console.addListener('login/platform', async function (platform, userId) {\n      const user = await ctx.database.getUser(platform, userId, ['id', 'name'])\n      if (!user) throw new Error('找不到此账户。')\n      if (this.auth?.id === user.id) throw new Error('你已经绑定了此账户。')\n\n      const key = `${platform}:${userId}`\n      const token = Math.random().toString().slice(2, 8)\n      const expiredAt = Date.now() + config.loginTokenExpire\n      states[key] = [token, expiredAt, this]\n\n      const listener = () => {\n        delete states[key]\n        dispose()\n        this.socket.removeEventListener('close', dispose)\n      }\n      const dispose = ctx.setTimeout(() => {\n        if (states[key]?.[1] >= Date.now()) listener()\n      }, config.loginTokenExpire)\n      this.socket.addEventListener('close', listener)\n\n      return { id: user.id, name: user.name, token, expiredAt }\n    })\n\n    ctx.middleware(async (session, next) => {\n      const state = states[session.uid]\n      if (!state || state[0] !== session.stripped.content) {\n        return next()\n      }\n\n      const { platform, userId: pid } = session\n      if (state[2].auth) {\n        await ctx.database.set('binding', { platform, pid }, { aid: state[2].auth.id })\n        return self.setAuth(state[2], state[2].auth)\n      } else {\n        const user = await session.observeUser(['id', 'name', 'authority', 'config'])\n        return self.createToken(state[2], 'platform', user)\n      }\n    }, true)\n\n    ctx.on('console/intercept', async (client, listener) => {\n      if (!listener.authority) return false\n      if (!client.auth) return true\n      if (client.auth.expiredAt <= Date.now()) return true\n      if (client.auth.authority < listener.authority) return true\n    })\n\n    ctx.console.addListener('user/delete-token', async function (inc) {\n      if (!this.auth) throw new Error('请先登录。')\n      const [data] = await ctx.database.get('token', { id: this.auth.id, inc })\n      if (!data) throw new Error('令牌不存在。')\n      await ctx.database.remove('token', { inc })\n      await self.setAuth(this)\n    })\n\n    ctx.console.addListener('user/logout', async function () {\n      if (this.auth) {\n        await ctx.database.remove('token', { token: this.auth.token })\n      }\n      await self.setAuth(this, null)\n    })\n\n    ctx.console.addListener('user/update', async function (data) {\n      if (!this.auth) throw new Error('请先登录。')\n      if (data.password) data.password = toHash(data.password)\n      await ctx.database.set('user', { id: this.auth.id }, data)\n      Object.assign(this.auth, data)\n      await self.setAuth(this, undefined, true)\n /root/koishi3/node_modules/@minatojs/sql.js/README.md:9:*sql.js* is a javascript SQL database. It allows you to create a relational database and query it entirely in the browser. You can try it in [this online demo](https://sql.js.org/examples/GUI/). It uses a [virtual database file stored in memory](https://emscripten.org/docs/porting/files/file_systems_overview.html), and thus **doesn't persist the changes** made to the database. However, it allows you to **import** any existing sqlite file, and to **export** the created database as a [JavaScript typed array](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Typed_arrays).
/root/koishi3/node_modules/@minatojs/sql.js/README.md:13:sql.js can be used like any traditional JavaScript library. If you are building a native application in JavaScript (using Electron for instance), or are working in node.js, you will likely prefer to use [a native binding of SQLite to JavaScript](https://www.npmjs.com/package/sqlite3). A native binding will not only be faster because it will run native code, but it will also be able to work on database files directly instead of having to load the entire database in memory, avoiding out of memory errors and further improving performances.

/root/koishi3/node_modules/leveldown/README.md:118:- `createIfMissing` (boolean, default: `true`): If `true`, will initialise an empty database at the specified location if one doesn't already exist. /root/koishi3/node_modules/leveldown/README.md:120:- `errorIfExists` (boolean, default: `false`): If `true`, you will receive an error in your `open()` callback if the database exists at the specified location.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/leveldown/README.md:132:> Larger values increase performance, especially during bulk loads. Up to two write buffers may be held in memory at the same time, so you may wish to adjust this parameter to control memory usage. Also, a larger write buffer will result in a longer recovery time the next time the database is opened.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/leveldown/README.md:142:> ... if your filesystem is more efficient with larger files, you could consider increasing the value. The downside will be longer compactions and hence longer latency/performance hiccups. Another reason to increase this parameter might be when you are initially populating a large database.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/leveldown/README.md:146:`close()` is an instance method on an existing database object. The underlying LevelDB database will be closed and the `callback` function will be called with no arguments if the operation is successful or with a single `error` argument if the operation failed for any reason.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/leveldown/README.md:229:`approximateSize()` is an instance method on an existing database object. Used to get the approximate number of bytes of file system space used by the range `[start..end)`. The result may not include recently written data.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/leveldown/README.md:237:`compactRange()` is an instance method on an existing database object. Used to manually trigger a database compaction in the range `[start..end)`.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/leveldown/README.md:253:- `leveldb.sstables`: returns a multi-line string describing all of the _sstables_ that make up contents of the current database.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/leveldown/README.md:367:Completely remove an existing LevelDB database directory. You can use this function in place of a full directory `rm` if you want to be sure to only remove LevelDB-related files. If the directory only contains LevelDB files, the directory itself will be removed as well. If there are additional, non-LevelDB files in the directory, those files, and the directory, will be left alone.

/root/koishi3/node_modules/cuid/README.md:75:Alternatively, you've played it safe and you only let your database create ids. Writes only happen on a master database, and load is spread out over read replicas. But with this kind of strain, you have to start scaling your database writes horizontally, too, and suddenly your application starts to crawl (if the db is smart enough to guarantee unique ids between write hosts), or you start getting id collisions between different db hosts, so your write hosts don't agree about which ids represent which data.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/cuid/README.md:82:Even worse, when the database is the only guarantee that ids are unique, that means that clients are forced to send incomplete records to the database, and wait for a network round-trip before they can use the ids in any algorithm. Forget about fast client performance. It simply isn't possible.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/cuid/README.md:84:That situation has caused some clients to create ids that are only usable in a single client session (such as an in-memory counter). When the database returns the real id, the client has to do some juggling logic to swap out the id being used.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/cuid/README.md:93:Monotonically increasing IDs are suitable for use as [high-performance database primary keys](http://code.openark.org/blog/mysql/monotonic-functions-sql-and-mysql), because they can be binary searched. Pure pseudo-random variants don't meet this requirement.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/cuid/README.md:103:Client-visible ids often need to have sufficient random data that it becomes practically impossible to try to guess valid IDs based on an existing, known id. That makes simple sequential ids unusable in the context of client-side generated database keys.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/cuid/README.md:122:Because cuids can be safely generated synchronously, you can generate a lot of them quickly. Since it's unlikely that you'll get a collision, you don't have to wait for a round trip to the database just to insert a complete record in your database.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/cuid/README.md:124:Because cuids are monotonically increasing, database primary key performance gets a significant boost.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/cuid/README.md:164:Need a smaller ID? `cuid.slug()` is for you. With 7 to 10 characters, `.slug()` is a great solution for short urls. Slugs may grow up to 10 characters as the internal counter increases. They're good for things like URL slug disambiguation (i.e., `example.com/some-post-title-<slug>`) but **absolutely not recommended for database unique IDs**. Stick to the full cuid for database keys.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/cuid/README.md:168:* are less likely to be monotonically increasing. Stick to full cuids for database lookups, if possible.
/root/koishi3/node_modules/cacheable-request/README.md:202:**Note:** Database connection errors are emitted here, however `cacheable-request` will attempt to re-request the resource and bypass the cache on a connection error. Therefore a database connection error doesn't necessarily mean the request won't be fulfilled.
